                  <hi rend="ital">Free, ingenuous,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">free-born; contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَبْدٌ</foreign>: (S, A, Mgh, Msb, K:) fem. <foreign lang="ar">حُرَّةٌ</foreign>: (S, Mgh, Msb, K:) pl. masc. <foreign lang="ar">أَحْرَارٌ</foreign> (Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">حِرَارٌ</foreign>; (IJ, K;) not <foreign lang="ar">حَرَارٌ</foreign>, as some say; nor is <foreign lang="ar">حِرَارٌ</foreign> an inf. n. as well as a pl., as others say: (MF:) pl. fem. <foreign lang="ar">حَرَائِرُ</foreign>, (Msb, K,) contr. to analogy, and, as Suh says, the only instance of the kind except <foreign lang="ar">شَجَرٌ مَرَائِرُ</foreign> as pl. of <foreign lang="ar">شَجَرَةٌ مُرَّةٌ</foreign>; for the [regular] pl. of <foreign lang="ar">فُعْلَةٌ</foreign> is <foreign lang="ar">فْعَلٌ</foreign>; but <foreign lang="ar">حُرَّةٌ</foreign> has this form of pl. because it is syn. with <foreign lang="ar">كَرِيمَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَقِيلَةٌ</foreign> [as will be seen in what follows]; and <foreign lang="ar">مُرَّةٌ</foreign>, because it means <foreign lang="ar">خَبِيثَةُ الطَّعْمِ</foreign>. (Msb.) Omar said to the women who used to go forth to the mosque, <foreign lang="ar">لَأَرُدَّنَّكْنَّ حَرَائِرَ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">I will assuredly make you to become free women</hi>]; meaning <hi rend="ital">I will assuredly make you to keep to the houses</hi>: for the curtain is lowered before free women; not before slavewomen. (TA.) [See also <foreign lang="ar">حُرِّيَّةٌ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Generous, noble,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">well-born;</hi> like as <foreign lang="ar">عَبْدٌ</foreign> is used to signify “ ignoble, ” or “ base-born: ” (Mgh:) and so the fem. <foreign lang="ar">حُرَّةٌ</foreign>; (S, Mgh, K;) applied to a woman; (TA;) and to a she-camel: (S:) and so the masc. applied to a horse. (K, TA.) [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">بَاتَتْ بِلَيْلَةِ حُرَّةٍ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">She passed a virgin's night</hi>] is said of her whose husband has not been able to devirginate her (S, A, K) in the night when she has been first brought to him: (TA:) because the <foreign lang="ar">حُرَّة</foreign> is modest and repugnant: (Har p. 418:) in the contr. case one says, <foreign lang="ar">بِلَيْلَةِ شَيْبَآءَ</foreign>: (S, L:) and one says also <foreign lang="ar">بِلَيْلَةٍ حُرَّةٍ</foreign>; and <foreign lang="ar">بِلَيْلَةٍ شَيْبَآءَ</foreign>. (TA.) [And hence,] <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلَةُ حُرَّة</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلَةٌ حُرَّةٌ</foreign> signify also <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The first night of the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">lunar</hi>] <hi rend="ital">month</hi>: (K:) its last night is called <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلَةُ شَيْبَآءَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلَةٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَيْبَآءُ</foreign>. (TA.) You say also <foreign lang="ar">وَجْهٌ حُرٌّ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [app. meaning <hi rend="ital">An ingenuous countenance</hi>]. (A.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Generous,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ingenuous, in conduct</hi>: as in the saying of Imra-el-Keys, <quote>

                  <foreign lang="ar">سَاقَ حُرَّ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">she calls</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ساق حرّ</foreign>]: on which IJ observes, As says, <foreign lang="ar">ساق حرّ</foreign> is thought to mean the young one of the bird; but it is her <hi rend="ital">cry:</hi> and he (IJ) adds, the fact that the poet [Sakhr] does not make it decl. is an evidence of the correctness of the assertion of As; for, were it decl., he would have said <foreign lang="ar">سَاقَ حُرٍّ</foreign> if it consisted of two nouns whereof the former was prefixed to the other so as to govern it in the gen. case, or <foreign lang="ar">ساق حُرًّا</foreign> if it were a compound; as it is indeterminate: and its being made decl. by Homeyd does not show it to be not significant of a sound; for sometimes an expression significant of a sound consists of two nouns whereof the former is prefixed to the latter so as to govern it in the gen. case, like <foreign lang="ar">خَازُ بَازٍ</foreign>.
